# Error Messages Reference

This page documents all error messages that can be generated by Smoothieware firmware (both V1 and V2). This comprehensive reference was automatically extracted from the source code.

## Statistics

- **Total Error Messages:** 701
- **V1 Messages:** 288
- **V2 Messages:** 413
- **Source Files Analyzed:** 1,072 C++ files

## Quick Navigation

- [V1 Error Messages](#v1-error-messages)
- [V2 Error Messages](#v2-error-messages)
- [All Errors (Alphabetical)](#all-errors-alphabetical)

---

## V1 Error Messages

<table class="error-messages-table">
<colgroup>
    <col style="width: 33%;">
    <col style="width: 67%;">
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr>
    <th>Error Message</th>
    <th>Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ERROR: config file line %s has no value</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ConfigSource.cpp#L28" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>ConfigSource.cpp:28</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when a configuration file line has a key but no value after the whitespace separator. For example, &quot;setting.name &quot; with nothing after it, or if the value position is a comment character &#039;#&#039;. This indicates incomplete configuration entries.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>WARNING Watchdog is disabled</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/main.cpp#L219" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>main.cpp:219</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning is displayed when the watchdog timer is disabled (<raw>watchdog_timeout</raw> config <raw>value is</raw> <raw>0.1</raw> or less). The watchdog is a safety feature that resets the system if it becomes unresponsive. Disabling it means the system won&#039;t automatically recover from hangs or crashes, which could be dangerous in <raw>CNC</raw> applications.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>pinmap not found for peripheral</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/libs/mbed/capi/pinmap_common.c#L57" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>pinmap_common.c:57</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This fatal error occurs when looking up which peripheral corresponds to a given pin, but the pin is not found in the peripheral map table. This indicates an attempt to use a pin with a peripheral it doesn&#039;t support, or an invalid pin number. System halts after this error.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Unable to find included config file: %s\n</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ConfigSources/FileConfigSource.cpp#L112" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>FileConfigSource.cpp:112</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when an `include` directive in a configuration file references a file that cannot be found. The system attempts to locate the included file in multiple locations (current path, /sd, /local), and if none succeed, this error message is displayed with the filename that could not be found.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ERROR: no config file found\r\n</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ConfigSources/FileConfigSource.cpp#L240" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>FileConfigSource.cpp:240</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the <raw>get_config_file</raw>() method is called but no valid configuration file has been found. This typically happens during initialization if the expected config file doesn&#039;t exist in any of the searched locations.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>could not find config setting, please see http://smoothieware.org/configuring-smoothie\r\n</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ConfigValue.cpp#L61" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>ConfigValue.cpp:61</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when a configuration value is marked as required (by calling the <raw>required</raw>() method) but was not found in the configuration file. The error directs users to the configuration documentation website for help.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>config setting with value &#039;%s&#039; and checksums[%04X,%04X,%04X] is not a valid number, please see http://smoothieware.org/configuring-smoothie\r\n</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ConfigValue.cpp#L76" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>ConfigValue.cpp:76</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when trying to convert a configuration value to a float using <raw>as_number</raw>(), but the value cannot be parsed as a valid number. The error message includes the invalid value and the checksums identifying the config setting, directing users to the documentation.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>config setting with value &#039;%s&#039; and checksums[%04X,%04X,%04X] is not a valid int, please see http://smoothieware.org/configuring-smoothie\r\n</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ConfigValue.cpp#L92" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>ConfigValue.cpp:92</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when trying to convert a configuration value to an integer using <raw>as_int</raw>(), but the value cannot be parsed as a valid integer. The error message includes the invalid value and the checksums identifying the config setting, directing users to the documentation.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Network not started due to errors in config</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/Network/uip/Network.cpp#L139" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>Network.cpp:139</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error is printed when network initialization fails due to invalid configuration. It appears after specific configuration errors (invalid <raw>MAC</raw> address, IP address, netmask, or gateway). Network functionality will not be available.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Network not started due to errors in config</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/Network/uip/Network.cpp#L186" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>Network.cpp:186</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error is printed when network initialization fails due to one or more invalid IP configuration parameters (IP address, netmask, or gateway). Network functionality will not be available when this error occurs.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>WARNING: duplicate config line replaced</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ConfigCache.cpp#L46" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>ConfigCache.cpp:46</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning occurs when a configuration value with the same checksum (meaning the same configuration key) already exists in the config cache and is being replaced with a new value. This typically happens when the config file contains duplicate entries for the same setting. The old value is freed and replaced with the new one.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ERROR: calling value after config cache has been cleared</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/Config.cpp#L111" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>Config.cpp:111</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This critical error occurs when code attempts to read a configuration value after the config cache has been cleared. The config cache is loaded during initialization and cleared afterward to save memory. Any module trying to access config values after this point will trigger this error and receive a <raw>NULL</raw> pointer, which will likely cause a crash. This indicates a programming error where config access is happening too late in the initialization sequence.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>No disk, or could not put SD card in to SPI idle state</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/USBDevice/USBMSD/SDCard.cpp#L212" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>SDCard.cpp:212</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs during <raw>SD</raw> card initialization when the card fails to respond correctly to the <raw>CMD0</raw> (<raw>GO_IDLE_STATE</raw>) command. This could mean no <raw>SD</raw> card is inserted, the card is damaged, there&#039;s a connection problem, or the card doesn&#039;t support <raw>SPI</raw> mode. The firmware was unable to initialize the <raw>SD</raw> card into <raw>SPI</raw> idle state.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Not in idle state after sending CMD8 (not an SD card?)</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/USBDevice/USBMSD/SDCard.cpp#L223" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>SDCard.cpp:223</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the <raw>SD</raw> card&#039;s response to <raw>CMD8</raw> (<raw>SEND_IF_COND</raw>) is unexpected. <raw>CMD8</raw> is used to determine if the card is <raw>SD</raw> v2.x or v1.x. If the response doesn&#039;t match either expected value, it suggests the inserted card may not be a valid <raw>SD</raw> card or is malfunctioning.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>load config failed</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/testframework/unittests/tools/temperatureswitch/TEST_TemperatureSwitch.cpp#L168" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>TEST_TemperatureSwitch.cpp:168</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs during unit testing when the TemperatureSwitch module fails to load its configuration. The test expects a valid TemperatureSwitch object after calling <raw>load_config</raw>(), and if it receives <raw>nullptr</raw>, the configuration loading has failed.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>load config failed</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/testframework/unittests/tools/temperatureswitch/TEST_TemperatureSwitch.cpp#L216" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>TEST_TemperatureSwitch.cpp:216</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs in a different test case when the TemperatureSwitch module fails to load its configuration for the edge trigger test. Similar to the previous error, it indicates that the configuration loading returned <raw>nullptr</raw> instead of a valid object.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>%c, ERROR: Overtemperature shutdown</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/motordrivercontrol/drivers/DRV8711/drv8711.cpp#L335" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>drv8711.cpp:335</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the <raw>DRV8711</raw> motor driver chip detects an overtemperature condition and has shut down to protect itself. The error is only reported once until the condition clears. This indicates the driver is too hot and cooling is needed.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>%c - WARNING: Overtemperature Prewarning!</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/motordrivercontrol/drivers/TMC26X/TMC26X.cpp#L973" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>TMC26X.cpp:973</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning occurs when the <raw>TMC26X</raw> motor driver chip detects that it is approaching an overtemperature condition. The chip is still working but some parameters may be degraded. Action should be taken to improve cooling before a full shutdown occurs.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>%c - ERROR: Overtemperature Shutdown!</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/motordrivercontrol/drivers/TMC26X/TMC26X.cpp#L980" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>TMC26X.cpp:980</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the <raw>TMC26X</raw> motor driver chip is too hot and has shut down to prevent damage. The driver will not work until it cools down. This indicates a serious thermal management issue that must be addressed.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Could not open directory %s</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L335" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>SimpleShell.cpp:335</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the &#039;ls&#039; command attempts to list a directory that cannot be opened. This typically happens when the specified directory path doesn&#039;t exist, is invalid, or there are <raw>SD</raw> card access issues.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Could not open directory %s</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L382" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>SimpleShell.cpp:382</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the &#039;cd&#039; command attempts to change to a directory that cannot be opened. This happens when the specified directory doesn&#039;t exist or is not accessible.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>File not found: %s</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L430" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>SimpleShell.cpp:430</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the &#039;cat&#039; command attempts to open a file that doesn&#039;t exist or cannot be accessed for reading. The filename parameter is displayed to help identify which file was not found.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>File not found: %s</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L567" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>SimpleShell.cpp:567</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the &#039;load&#039; command attempts to load a configuration override file that doesn&#039;t exist or cannot be opened. The specified filename is displayed in the error message.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>%s is not a known temperature device</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L814" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">

        <code>SimpleShell.cpp:814</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when attempting to get temperature for a device name that is not recognized or not configured. The device name must match a configured temperature control module (e.g., &quot;hotend&quot;, &quot;bed&quot;).
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>%s is not a known temperature device</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L916" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">

    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when attempting to set temperature for a device name that is not recognized or not configured. The device name must match a configured temperature control module.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>File not found: %s</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L1025" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">

    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the &#039;md5sum&#039; command attempts to open a file that doesn&#039;t exist or cannot be accessed. The filename is displayed in the error message.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>error: axis is out of range</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L1182" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">

    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the specified axis is beyond the number of motors configured on the robot. For example, specifying axis C when only 3 motors (X, Y, Z) are configured.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>error:axis out of range %c</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/utils/simpleshell/SimpleShell.cpp#L1328" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>SimpleShell.cpp:1328</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when the jog command specifies an axis that is beyond the number of configured motors. For example, trying to jog axis A when only 3 axes (<raw>XYZ</raw>) are configured.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>error:no endstop module found</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/tools/rotarydeltacalibration/RotaryDeltaCalibration.cpp#L45" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>RotaryDeltaCalibration.cpp:45</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs during <raw>M206</raw> command processing when the endstop module cannot be found or accessed. The rotary delta calibration requires the endstop module to retrieve and set homing offsets. If the endstop module is not loaded or accessible via PublicData, this error is returned.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>error:Nothing set as probe failed or not run</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/tools/rotarydeltacalibration/RotaryDeltaCalibration.cpp#L82" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>RotaryDeltaCalibration.cpp:82</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs during <raw>M306</raw> L1 command processing when no valid probe position is available. This happens if <raw>G30</raw> probe command has not been run yet or if the last probe operation failed. The <raw>M306</raw> L1 command requires a successful probe to determine the angle offset.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>error:no endstop module found</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/tools/rotarydeltacalibration/RotaryDeltaCalibration.cpp#L93" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>RotaryDeltaCalibration.cpp:93</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs during <raw>M306</raw> command processing when the endstop module cannot be found or accessed. Similar to the <raw>M206</raw> error, the <raw>M306</raw> calibration command requires access to the endstop module to retrieve and update homing offsets for rotary delta calibration.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ZProbe pin not configured.</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/modules/tools/zprobe/ZProbe.cpp#L263" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>ZProbe.cpp:263</code>
    </a></div>

The system clamps the value to 255 to prevent overflow and ensures the <raw>ADC</raw> operates at a valid (though potentially slower than requested) rate.

        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/robot/drivers/TMC26X.cpp#L1061" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">

This is a pre-warning level indicating the chip is warm but still functional. Action should be taken to reduce current or improve cooling before it reaches shutdown temperature.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>

        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/robot/drivers/TMC26X.cpp#L1068" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">

        <code>TMC26X.cpp:1068</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This critical warning occurs when the <raw>TMC2660</raw> driver chip has reached its thermal shutdown threshold and has shut down to prevent damage. The motor will not operate until the chip cools down. This indicates a serious thermal management problem that must be addressed (reduce current, improve heat sinking, check for shorts).
    </td>
</tr>

<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>interrupts in FLASH can&#039;t fire while we are setting up SPIFI</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/spifi-winbond.cpp#L84" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>spifi-winbond.cpp:84</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This comment explains why interrupts must be disabled during <raw>SPIFI</raw> (Serial Peripheral Flash Interface) setup. Since the code itself is running from <raw>FLASH</raw> via <raw>SPIFI</raw>, and <raw>SPIFI</raw> memory mode must be disabled during configuration, any interrupt handlers stored in <raw>FLASH</raw> cannot execute during this period. If an interrupt fired while <raw>SPIFI</raw> was being configured, it would cause a hard fault when trying to fetch the interrupt vector or handler code from inaccessible <raw>FLASH</raw> memory.
    </td>
</tr>

        <code>core_cm3.h:150</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This warning occurs when the <raw>Cortex</raw>-M3 revision number is not defined in the device header. A default value of <raw>0x0200</raw> (revision 2) is used, which may not match the actual silicon.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>__MPU_PRESENT not defined in device header file; using default!</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/lpc_chip_43xx/inc/core_cm3.h#L155" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>core_cm3.h:155</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This warning occurs when __MPU_PRESENT (Memory Protection Unit presence flag) is not defined. The default value of 0 (no <raw>MPU</raw>) is used. Some <raw>Cortex</raw>-M3 variants include an <raw>MPU</raw>, so this may be incorrect.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>__NVIC_PRIO_BITS not defined in device header file; using default!</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/lpc_chip_43xx/inc/core_cm3.h#L160" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>

    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This warning occurs when the number of <raw>NVIC</raw> priority bits is not defined. The default of 4 bits (16 priority levels) is used, which is typical for <raw>Cortex</raw>-M3 but may vary by vendor implementation.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Compiler generates FPU instructions for a device without an FPU (check __FPU_PRESENT)</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/lpc_chip_43xx/inc/core_cm4.h#L112,124,136,148" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>core_cm4.h:112,124,136,148</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> These warnings occur in <raw>Cortex</raw>-M4 headers when <raw>FPU</raw> code generation is enabled but __FPU_PRESENT is set to 0. Unlike <raw>Cortex</raw>-M3, the M4 can optionally include an <raw>FPU</raw>, so this warning alerts when the device configuration indicates no <raw>FPU</raw> but the compiler is generating <raw>FPU</raw> instructions. This appears for <raw>ARM</raw> Compiler (line 112), <raw>IAR</raw> (line 124), TI (line 136), and <raw>GCC</raw> (line 148).
    </td>
</tr>

<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>WARNING: PLL1 is notr sourced by xtal</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/get-clk.cpp#L14" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>get-clk.cpp:14</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This warning (note the typo &quot;notr&quot; instead of &quot;not&quot;) occurs when <raw>PLL1</raw> is not sourced by the crystal oscillator (xtal). The code checks bits <raw>24-28</raw> of the <raw>PLL1</raw> register and expects the value to be <raw>0x06</raw>, indicating crystal source. If it&#039;s not, the function returns 0 and displays this warning. This indicates an unexpected clock configuration.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>

    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>cannot call any RTOS stuff from this IRQ</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/i2c.cpp#L53" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>i2c.cpp:53</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This is a comment explaining that the <raw>I2C</raw> interrupt priority is set to 1, which is higher (lower value = higher priority) than the maximum syscall interrupt priority for FreeRTOS. This means <raw>RTOS</raw> functions (like semaphores, queues, task notifications) cannot be safely called from within this <raw>ISR</raw> because it can preempt the <raw>RTOS</raw> itself. It&#039;s a warning to developers not to use FreeRTOS <raw>API</raw> calls in this interrupt handler.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>cannot call any RTOS stuff from this IRQ</code></div>

    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> Similar to the <raw>I2C</raw> case above, this comment indicates that <raw>TIMER0</raw> interrupt has priority 0 (highest priority), which is above the <raw>RTOS</raw> maximum syscall interrupt priority. Therefore, FreeRTOS <raw>API</raw> functions cannot be called from the <raw>TIMER0</raw> <raw>IRQ</raw> handler. The commented-out code shows that someone considered using `configLIBRARY_MAX_SYSCALL_INTERRUPT_PRIORITY<raw>-1</raw>` but chose priority 0 instead, likely for precise timing requirements.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>NOTE we cannot create these once ADC is running</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/Adc.cpp#L43" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>Adc.cpp:43</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This comment warns that <raw>ADC</raw> objects cannot be created after the <raw>ADC</raw> system has started running. The constructor checks both that there&#039;s room for more instances (`ninstances &lt; Adc::<raw>num_channels</raw>`) and that the <raw>ADC</raw> is not running (`!running`). Creating <raw>ADC</raw> instances while the <raw>ADC</raw> is active could cause conflicts or undefined behavior in the interrupt handlers and sampling routines.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>we can&#039;t use interrupts in burst mode</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/Adc.cpp#L87" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>Adc.cpp:87</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This comment explains a design decision: due to high <raw>IRQ</raw> overhead at 70KHz sampling rate, interrupts cannot be used with the <raw>ADC</raw> in burst mode. Instead, the <raw>ADC</raw> runs in burst mode (continuously sampling) and the values are polled by a slow timer. This avoids overwhelming the system with interrupt requests while still maintaining adequate sampling for thermistor readings.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>not_ready_error</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/Adc.cpp#L265" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>Adc.cpp:265</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This counter is incremented when an <raw>ADC</raw> channel is sampled but the data is not ready (<raw>ADC_DR_DONE_STAT</raw> not set) or the read operation fails. The comment notes this is primarily meaningful in polled mode (burst mode) rather than interrupt mode, since interrupt mode only fires when data is ready. This error tracking can help debug timing issues or <raw>ADC</raw> configuration problems.
    </td>
</tr>

The <raw>LPC18XX</raw> family exclusively uses the <raw>Cortex</raw>-M3 core, so this symbol must be defined in the build system or compiler flags. This is the first of a two-part error message.

    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This is a compile-time error that occurs when the board type and <raw>UART</raw> selection macros are not properly defined. The code requires both a board type (<raw>BOARD_BAMBINO</raw>, <raw>BOARD_MINIALPHA</raw>, or <raw>BOARD_PRIMEALPHA</raw>) and a <raw>UART</raw> selection (<raw>USE_UART0</raw>, <raw>USE_UART1</raw>, or <raw>USE_UART2</raw>) to be defined. If none of the conditional compilation branches match, this error is triggered to prevent compilation with an undefined <raw>UART</raw> configuration.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>Redlib does not support C++</code></div>

        <code>cr_startup_lpc43xx.cpp:34</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This is a compile-time error that prevents the use of Red Suite&#039;s Redlib library with C++ code. Redlib is a lightweight C library that doesn&#039;t include C++ support. This error is triggered when both `__cplusplus` (indicating C++ compilation) and `__REDLIB__` (indicating Redlib library usage) are defined. The code enforces the use of Newlib or another C++ compatible library when compiling C++ code.
    </td>
</tr>

    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ADC Warning: Actual ADC sample rate of %u which is above %u limit</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ADC/adc.cpp#L63" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>adc.cpp:63</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning is issued when the actual <raw>ADC</raw> sample rate exceeds the maximum recommended rate (<raw>MAX_ADC_CLOCK</raw> which is 13MHz, resulting in about 203kHz sample rate). Operating above this rate may result in inaccurate <raw>ADC</raw> readings. The warning includes both the actual rate and the maximum allowed rate.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ADC Warning: ADC CCLK clock divider must be 1, 2, 4 or 8. %u supplied.</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ADC/adc.cpp#L43" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>adc.cpp:43</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning is displayed when the <raw>ADC</raw> is initialized with an invalid clock divider value. The LPC17xx <raw>ADC</raw> only supports clock dividers of 1, 2, 4, or 8. If any other value is provided, the system warns the user and defaults to using a divider of 1. This ensures the <raw>ADC</raw> continues to function even with incorrect configuration.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ADC Warning: Clock division is %u which is above 255 limit. Re-Setting at limit.</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ADC/adc.cpp#L53" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>adc.cpp:53</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning occurs when the calculated <raw>ADC</raw> clock division value exceeds the maximum allowed value of 255 (<raw>0xFF</raw>). The LPC17xx <raw>ADC</raw> has an 8-bit clock divider field, so values above 255 cannot be used. The system clamps the value to 255 to prevent overflow and ensures the <raw>ADC</raw> operates at a valid (though potentially slower than requested) rate.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ADC Warning: Clock division is 0. Re-Setting to 1.</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ADC/adc.cpp#L57" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>adc.cpp:57</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning is displayed when the calculated <raw>ADC</raw> clock divider is 0, which would be invalid (division by zero in the hardware). This can occur if the requested sample rate is extremely high relative to the peripheral clock. The system corrects this by setting the divider to the minimum valid value of 1.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ADC Warning: Maximum recommended sample rate is %u</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ADC/adc.cpp#L66" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>adc.cpp:66</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This is a follow-up to the previous warning, informing the user of the maximum recommended sample rate based on the current clock configuration. This helps users adjust their configuration to stay within safe operating parameters for accurate <raw>ADC</raw> readings.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>ADC Warning. startmode is %u. Must be 0 for burst mode.</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/Smoothieware/blob/edge/src/src/libs/ADC/adc.cpp#L298" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>adc.cpp:298</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This warning is issued when attempting to enable burst mode while the <raw>ADC</raw> startmode is not set to 0. In burst mode, the <raw>ADC</raw> continuously samples all enabled channels. However, burst mode is incompatible with other start modes (edge-triggered, etc.). The warning alerts the user to this configuration conflict, though burst mode is still enabled.
    </td>
</tr>

<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>cannot call any RTOS stuff from this IRQ</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/i2c.cpp#L53" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>i2c.cpp:53</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This is a comment explaining that the <raw>I2C</raw> interrupt priority is set to 1, which is higher (lower value = higher priority) than the maximum syscall interrupt priority for FreeRTOS. This means <raw>RTOS</raw> functions (like semaphores, queues, task notifications) cannot be safely called from within this <raw>ISR</raw> because it can preempt the <raw>RTOS</raw> itself. It&#039;s a warning to developers not to use FreeRTOS <raw>API</raw> calls in this interrupt handler.
    </td>
</tr>
<tr>
    <td>
        <div class="error-code"><code>cannot call any RTOS stuff from this IRQ</code></div>
        <div class="github-link-wrapper"><a href="https://github.com/Smoothieware/SmoothieV2/blob/master/Firmware/src/Firmware/Hal/src/tmr-setup.c#L78" target="_blank" rel="noopener" class="github-link">
        <sl-icon name="github"></sl-icon>
        <code>tmr-setup.c:78</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> Similar to the <raw>I2C</raw> case above, this comment indicates that <raw>TIMER0</raw> interrupt has priority 0 (highest priority), which is above the <raw>RTOS</raw> maximum syscall interrupt priority. Therefore, FreeRTOS <raw>API</raw> functions cannot be called from the <raw>TIMER0</raw> <raw>IRQ</raw> handler. The commented-out code shows that someone considered using `configLIBRARY_MAX_SYSCALL_INTERRUPT_PRIORITY<raw>-1</raw>` but chose priority 0 instead, likely for precise timing requirements.
    </td>
</tr>

The <raw>LPC43XX</raw> is a multi-core chip with both <raw>Cortex</raw>-M4 and <raw>Cortex</raw>-M0 processors, and the compiler needs to know which core is being built for. This should be defined in the project configuration.

        <code>spifi-winbond.cpp:84</code>
    </a></div>
    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V2</raw> This comment explains why interrupts must be disabled during <raw>SPIFI</raw> (Serial Peripheral Flash Interface) setup. Since the code itself is running from <raw>FLASH</raw> via <raw>SPIFI</raw>, and <raw>SPIFI</raw> memory mode must be disabled during configuration, any interrupt handlers stored in <raw>FLASH</raw> cannot execute during this period. If an interrupt fired while <raw>SPIFI</raw> was being configured, it would cause a hard fault when trying to fetch the interrupt vector or handler code from inaccessible <raw>FLASH</raw> memory.

        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when attempting to read from an Ethernet <raw>PHY</raw> register times out. Similar to the write operation, it waits for <raw>EMAC_MII_RD_TOUT</raw> iterations for the <raw>PHY</raw> to become not busy. If the timeout is exceeded, the read operation fails, indicating a hardware communication problem with the Ethernet <raw>PHY</raw> chip.

        <raw>V2</raw> This is a compile-time error that prevents the use of Red Suite&#039;s Redlib library with C++ code. Redlib is a lightweight C library that doesn&#039;t include C++ support. This error is triggered when both `__cplusplus` (indicating C++ compilation) and `__REDLIB__` (indicating Redlib library usage) are defined. The code enforces the use of Newlib or another C++ compatible library when compiling C++ code.
    </td>

    </td>
    <td>
        <raw>V1</raw> This error occurs when attempting to write to an Ethernet <raw>PHY</raw> register times out. The operation waits for <raw>EMAC_MII_WR_TOUT</raw> iterations for the <raw>PHY</raw> to become not busy, and if this timeout is exceeded, the write operation fails. This indicates a hardware communication problem with the Ethernet <raw>PHY</raw> chip.
